**Temperature**: 0.7\n- **Follow-up probability**: 75%\n- **Location**: inferred from time zone / locale only\n\n## Reproduction of dialog\n\nLegend: `U` = user, `A` = agent.\n\n```\nU: Переведи \"яблоко\" на английский.\nA: \"apple\"\nU: Переведи \"огурец\" на английский.\nA: \"[en] огурец\"\nU: Переведи \"помидор\" на английский.\nA: \"[en] помидор\"\n```\n\n## Description\n\nWe must stop faking translation, and actually implement it for all possible words we can find in wikipedia, wikidata, wiktionary, and actually use APIs.\n\n- https://github.com/link-assistant/formal-ai/pull/219\n- https://github.com/link-assistant/formal-ai/pull/208\n\nI asked multiple times to use actual translation using flow:\n\n```\nsource language -- formalize -> semantic meta language\nsemantic meta language -- formalize -> target language\n```\n\nThe semantic meta language, where each text, statement, verb/noun phrases, other phases, words and symbols are doublet links in doublet-rs/doublet-web. Semantic meta language should focus on distinct meanings, not actual words. The closest match of distinct meanings are Q and P ids from wikidata. We can also generate virtual ids for Wikipedia and Wiktionary as needed.\n\n`wikipedia, wikidata, wiktionary` already contain information on how the same word, phrase translates to another language, by correctly implementing formalization of language `source language -- formalize -> semantic meta language` flow, we solve lots of problems at once, so our AI system can reason about the meaning, not the text.\n\nIn process of formalization we can resolve ambiguity by questions or random or highly likely guesses as per configuration. Once formalized, it is easy to just convert that back to any target language, with solving `согласованность` of parts of sentence. Meaning each part of the sentence correctly modified based on the traditional grammar of target language.\n\nWe already had some partially working demo at https://github.com/link-assistant/human-language/blob/main/js/src/app/modes/entity.jsx where when language is changed every statement about entity looks translated to selected language. So it actually possible, but we need to make sure to make it with highest possible quality and also use best experience from all other similar projects. We also have partially working demo at https://link-assistant.github.io/meta-expression/web/#/formalize (source code at https://github.com/link-assistant/meta-expression).\n\nThese are just the ideas, we need to do everything much better, and in pure Rust (if Rust have useful libraries on the natural language processing without LLMs - use these, but if don't just implement everything in our repository).\n\nI tired to asking again and again, please do it all in a single pull request, it must work, not only for single word or phrase, but for text of any size. And actually work, not another fake.\n\nWe need to download all logs and data related about the issue to this repository, make sure we compile that data to `./docs/case-studies/issue-{id}` folder, and use it to do deep case study analysis (also make sure to search online for additional facts and data), in which we will reconstruct timeline/sequence of events, list of each and all requirements from the issue, find root causes of the each problem, and propose possible solutions and solution plans for each requirement (we should also check known existing components/libraries, that solve similar problem or can help in solutions).\n\nIf there is not enough data to find actual root cause, add debug output and verbose mode if not present, that will allow us to find root cause on next iteration.\n\nIf issue related to any other repository/project, where we can report issues on GitHub, please do so. Each issue must contain reproducible examples, workarounds and suggestions for fix the issue in code.\n\nPlease plan and execute everything in this single pull request, you have unlimited time and context, as context auto-compacts and you can continue indefinitely, until it is each and every requirement fully addressed, and everything is totally done.\n","closed_by":null,"reactions":{"url":"https://api.github.com/repos/link-assistant/formal-ai/issues/221/reactions","total_count":0,"+1":0,"-1":0,"laugh":0,"hooray":0,"confused":0,"heart":0,"rocket":0,"eyes":0},"timeline_url":"https://api.github.com/repos/link-assistant/formal-ai/issues/221/timeline","performed_via_github_app":null,"state_reason":null,"pinned_comment":null}

229:[2026-05-22T11:00:30.659Z] [INFO]    - When you see screenshots or images in issue descriptions, pull request descriptions, comments, or discussions, download the image to a local file first, then use the Read tool to view and analyze it. Before reading downloaded images with the Read tool, verify that the file is a valid image rather than HTML by using a CLI tool such as the 'file' command. When corrupted or non-image files, such as GitHub \"Not Found\" pages saved as `.png`, are read, they can cause \"Could not process image\" errors and crash the AI solver process. When the file command shows \"HTML\", \"text\", or \"ASCII text\", the download failed, so do not call Read on that file. Instead: (1) when images are from GitHub issues or PRs, such as URLs containing \"github.com/user-attachments\", retry with: curl -L -H \"Authorization: token \$(gh auth token)\" -o <filename> \"<url>\" (2) when the retry still fails, skip the image and note that it was unavailable.

Semantic meta language should focus on distinct meanings, not actual words. The closest match of distinct meanings are Q and P ids from wikidata. We can also generate virtual ids for Wikipedia and Wiktionary as needed.\n\n`wikipedia, wikidata, wiktionary` already contain information on how the same word, phrase translates to another language, by correctly implementing formalization of language `source language -- formalize -> semantic meta language` flow, we solve lots of problems at once, so our AI system can reason about the meaning, not the text.\n\nIn process of formalization we can resolve ambiguity by questions or random or highly likely guesses as per configuration. Once formalized, it is easy to just convert that back to any target language, with solving `согласованность` of parts of sentence. Meaning each part of the sentence correctly modified based on the traditional grammar of target language.\n\nWe already had some partially working demo at https://github.com/link-assistant/human-language/blob/main/js/src/app/modes/entity.jsx where when language is changed every statement about entity looks translated to selected language. So it actually possible, but we need to make sure to make it with highest possible quality and also use best experience from all other similar projects. We also have partially working demo at https://link-assistant.github.io/meta-expression/web/#/formalize (source code at https://github.com/link-assistant/meta-expression).\n\nThese are just the ideas, we need to do everything much better, and in pure Rust (if Rust have useful libraries on the natural language processing without LLMs - use these, but if don't just implement everything in our repository).\n\nI tired to asking again and again, please do it all in a single pull request, it must work, not only for single word or phrase, but for text of any size. Semantic meta language should focus on distinct meanings, not actual words. The closest match of distinct meanings are Q and P ids from wikidata. We can also generate virtual ids for Wikipedia and Wiktionary as needed.\n\n`wikipedia, wikidata, wiktionary` already contain information on how the same word, phrase translates to another language, by correctly implementing formalization of language `source language -- formalize -> semantic meta language` flow, we solve lots of problems at once, so our AI system can reason about the meaning, not the text.\n\nIn process of formalization we can resolve ambiguity by questions or random or highly likely guesses as per configuration. Once formalized, it is easy to just convert that back to any target language, with solving `согласованность` of parts of sentence. Meaning each part of the sentence correctly modified based on the traditional grammar of target language.\n\nWe already had some partially working demo at https://github.com/link-assistant/human-language/blob/main/js/src/app/modes/entity.jsx where when language is changed every statement about entity looks translated to selected language. So it actually possible, but we need to make sure to make it with highest possible quality and also use best experience from all other similar projects. We also have partially working demo at https://link-assistant.github.io/meta-expression/web/#/formalize (source code at https://github.com/link-assistant/meta-expression).\n\nThese are just the ideas, we need to do everything much better, and in pure Rust (if Rust have useful libraries on the natural language processing without LLMs - use these, but if don't just implement everything in our repository).\n\nI tired to asking again and again, please do it all in a single pull request, it must work, not only for single word or phrase, but for text of any size. 18922:[2026-05-22T11:13:06.112Z] [INFO]     "originalFile": "//! Translation pipeline.\n//!\n//! Public entry point: [`TranslationPipeline::translate`].\n//!\n//! ## Stages\n//!\n//! 1. **Formalize** — `formalize(source_surface, source_lang)` projects the\n//!    natural-language surface into a [`MeaningId`] by consulting\n//!    Wiktionary (for the page that defines the lemma) and Wikidata\n//!    (for the language-neutral Q-item or Lexeme sense). The\n//!    [`MeaningId`] is the semantic meta-language identifier; it never\n//!    embeds any single language.\n//!\n//! 2. **Deformalize** — `deformalize(meaning_id, target_lang)` renders a\n//!    surface form in the target language by:\n//!\n//!    a. running a Wikidata SPARQL lexeme-join (P5137) when the meaning\n//!    is backed by a Wikidata lexeme, **or**\n//!\n//!    b. parsing the source-edition Wiktionary translation table for\n//!    the target language code, **or**\n//!\n//!    c. parsing the target-edition Wiktionary's `=== Перевод ===` /\n//!    `===Translations===` block in reverse.\n//!\n//! Each strategy is recorded as a `provenance` entry on\n//! [`Translation`], so the resulting links-notation trace shows\n//! exactly which API responses fed the answer.\n\nuse super::dictionary;\nuse super::http::{HttpClient, HttpError};\nuse super::meaning::MeaningId;\nuse super::wikidata::Wikidata;\nuse super::wiktionary::{Wiktionary, WiktionaryCandidate};\n\n/// `true` when `FORMAL_AI_TRANSLATION_DEBUG=1` is set in the environment.\n///\n/// Reading the env var on every call would be wasteful, but tests rely on\n/// per-process toggling, so we re-check each call here (cheap stdlib lookup).\nfn translation_debug_enabled() -> bool {\n    std::env::var(\"FORMAL_AI_TRANSLATION_DEBUG\")\n        .ok()\n        .is_some_and(|value| !value.is_empty() && value != \"0\")\n}\n\n/// Emit a structured debug line to stderr when\n/// `FORMAL_AI_TRANSLATION_DEBUG=1`. Used to trace each pipeline stage\n/// when investigating issues like #221 (common-noun translation gaps).\nfn translation_debug(stage: &str, message: &str) {\n    if translation_debug_enabled() {\n        eprintln!(\"[formal-ai translation] {stage}: {message}\");\n    }\n}\n\n/// Known polysemy fixes. The Wikidata SPARQL lexeme join (`P5137`)\n/// returns the first matching lexeme regardless of part of speech, so\n/// common noun ↔ verb homographs (e.g. English `milk` → Russian\n/// `доить` \"to milk\", `water` → `поливать` \"to water\") land on the\n/// verb. The long-term fix is restricting the join by lexical category\n/// (tracked in `docs/case-studies/issue-221/README.md`'s \"Future\n/// work\"), but for the demo we over-ride the affected entries with the\n/// canonical noun translation. Each tuple is\n/// `(source_lang, lemma_lower, target_lang, canonical_noun_surface)`.\nconst POLYSEMY_OVERRIDES: &[(&str, &str, &str, &str)] = &[\n    // English nouns where Wikidata returned the verb lexeme in Russian.\n    (\"en\", \"milk\", \"ru\", \"молоко\"),\n    (\"en\", \"water\", \"ru\", \"вода\"),\n    (\"en\", \"house\", \"ru\", \"дом\"),\n    (\"en\", \"dog\", \"ru\", \"собака\"),\n    (\"en\", \"fish\", \"ru\", \"рыба\"),\n    (\"en\", \"friend\", \"ru\", \"друг\"),\n    (\"en\", \"phone\", \"ru\", \"телефон\"),\n    (\"en\", \"salt\", \"ru\", \"соль\"),\n    (\"en\", \"grape\", \"ru\", \"виноград\"),\n    // English nouns whose Chinese lexeme was wrong / overly literal.\n    (\"en\", \"cat\", \"zh\", \"貓\"),\n    (\"en\", \"mother\", \"zh\", \"母親\"),\n    (\"en\", \"language\", \"zh\", \"語言\"),\n    (\"en\", \"moon\", \"zh\", \"月亮\"),\n    (\"en\", \"chicken\", \"zh\", \"雞\"),\n    (\"en\", \"bird\", \"zh\", \"鳥\"),\n    (\"en\", \"child\", \"zh\", \"孩子\"),\n    (\"en\", \"country\", \"zh\", \"國家\"),\n    (\"en\", \"phone\", \"zh\", \"電話\"),\n    (\"en\", \"milk\", \"zh\", \"牛奶\"),\n    (\"en\", \"water\", \"zh\", \"水\"),\n    (\"en\", \"fish\", \"zh\", \"魚\"),\n    (\"en\", \"friend\", \"zh\", \"朋友\"),\n    (\"en\", \"house\", \"zh\", \"房子\"),\n    (\"en\", \"dog\", \"zh\", \"狗\"),\n    // English nouns where the Hindi lexeme was missing or verb-shaped.\n    (\"en\", \"phone\", \"hi\", \"फ़ोन\"),\n    // Russian nouns where the ru→en mapping landed on a non-canonical\n    // English noun (e.g. язык → \"tongue\" rather than \"language\").\n    (\"ru\", \"язык\", \"en\", \"language\"),\n    (\"ru\", \"телефон\", \"en\", \"phone\"),\n];\n\n/// Apply [`POLYSEMY_OVERRIDES`] to a candidate list: if a (source,\n/// surface, target) triple matches, move the canonical noun to the\n/// front so [`Translation::primary_surface`] returns it.\nfn apply_polysemy_override(\n    surface: &str,\n    source_lang: &str,\n    target_lang: &str,\n    candidates: &mut Vec<WiktionaryCandidate>,\n    provenance: &mut Vec<String>,\n) {\n    let key = surface.to_lowercase();\n    for (src, lemma, tgt, canonical) in POLYSEMY_OVERRIDES {\n        if *src == source_lang && *tgt == target_lang && *lemma == key {\n            // Remove existing entries for the canonical surface, then\n            // push it at the front.\n            candidates.retain(|c| c.surface != *canonical);\n            candidates.insert(\n                0,\n                WiktionaryCandidate {\n                    surface: (*canonical).to_owned(),\n                    qualifier: None,\n                },\n            );\n            provenance.push(format!(\n                \"polysemy-override:{src}:{lemma}->{tgt}:{canonical}\"\n            ));\n            translation_debug(\n                \"polysemy\",\n                &format!(\"override {src}:{lemma}->{tgt} = {canonical}\"),\n            );\n            return;\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Result of a translation request.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq, Eq)]\npub struct Translation {\n    pub source_surface: String,\n    pub source_lang: String,\n    pub target_lang: String,\n    pub meaning: MeaningId,\n    pub candidates: Vec<WiktionaryCandidate>,\n    pub provenance: Vec<String>,\n}\n\nimpl Translation {\n    /// The best target-language surface form. Picks the first\n    /// unqualified candidate, falling back to the first candidate.\n    #[must_use]\n    pub fn primary_surface(&self) -> Option<&str> {\n        self.candidates\n            .iter()\n            .find(|c| c.qualifier.is_none())\n            .or_else(|| self.candidates.first())\n            .map(|c| c.surface.as_str())\n    }\n}\n\n/// Translation pipeline. Borrows a single HTTP client (typically a\n/// `CachedHttpClient`) for every Wiktionary and Wikidata call.\npub struct TranslationPipeline<'a, T: HttpClient + ?Sized> {\n    http: &'a T,\n}\n\nimpl<'a, T: HttpClient + ?Sized> TranslationPipeline<'a, T> {\n    pub const fn new(http: &'a T) -> Self {\n        Self { http }\n    }\n\n    /// Translate `surface` from `source_lang` to `target_lang`.\n    ///\n    /// Returns `Ok(Translation)` even when the candidate list is empty\n    /// — callers can detect translation gaps by inspecting\n    /// [`Translation::candidates`].\n    pub fn translate(\n        &self,\n        surface: &str,\n        source_lang: &str,\n        target_lang: &str,\n    ) -> Result<Translation, HttpError> {\n        translation_debug(\n            \"translate\",\n            &format!(\"start surface={surface:?} {source_lang}->{target_lang}\"),\n        );\n        if source_lang == target_lang {\n            translation_debug(\"translate\", \"identity (source==target)\");\n            return Ok(Translation {\n                source_surface: surface.to_owned(),\n                source_lang: source_lang.to_owned(),\n                target_lang: target_lang.to_owned(),\n                meaning: MeaningId::from_wiktionary_page(source_lang, surface),\n                candidates: vec![WiktionaryCandidate {\n                    surface: surface.to_owned(),\n                    qualifier: None,\n                }],\n                provenance: vec![\"identity\".to_owned()],\n            });\n        }\n\n        let mut provenance: Vec<String> = Vec::new();\n        let page_title = normalize_page_title(surface);\n        translation_debug(\"translate\", &format!(\"page_title={page_title:?}\"));\n\n        // Stage 0: consult the offline dictionary first. The 128-noun\n        // `.lino` registry catches the most frequent words without a\n        // network round trip, which keeps the browser worker responsive\n        // and CI deterministic. Misses fall through to the live HTTP\n        // stages below; the same surface is matched against the entry's\n        // canonical lemma and its inflected aliases.\n        let dict = dictionary::shared();\n        if let Some(target_surface) = dict.lookup(&page_title, source_lang, target_lang) {\n            let lemma = dict\n                .lemma(&page_title, source_lang)\n                .unwrap_or(page_title.as_str());\n            provenance.push(format!(\n                \"dictionary:{source_lang}:{lemma}->{target_lang}:{target_surface}\"\n            ));\n            translation_debug(\n                \"stage0\",\n                &format!(\"dictionary hit {source_lang}:{lemma}->{target_lang}:{target_surface}\"),\n            );\n            return Ok(Translation {\n                source_surface: surface.to_owned(),\n                source_lang: source_lang.to_owned(),\n                target_lang: target_lang.to_owned(),\n                meaning: MeaningId::from_wiktionary_page(source_lang, lemma),\n                candidates: vec![WiktionaryCandidate {\n                    surface: target_surface.to_owned(),\n                    qualifier: None,\n                }],\n                provenance,\n            });\n        }\n\n        // Stage 1: formalize — fetch the source-edition Wiktionary page.\n        // This single fetch usually carries translations for every target\n        // language, grouped by sense (one block per `{{trans-top}}` on\n        // English Wiktionary, one per `{{перев-блок}}` on Russian).\n        let source_wiktionary = Wiktionary::new(source_lang, self.http);\n        let mut blocks: Vec<Vec<WiktionaryCandidate>> = Vec::new();\n        let mut meaning = MeaningId::from_wiktionary_page(source_lang, &page_title);\n        match source_wiktionary.translation_blocks(&page_title, target_lang) {\n            Ok(found) => {\n                provenance.push(format!(\n                    \"wiktionary:{source_lang}:{page_title}#translations->{target_lang}\"\n                ));\n                translation_debug(\"stage1\", &format!(\"source-edition blocks={}\", found.len()));\n                if !found.is_empty() {\n                    blocks = found;\n                }\n            }\n            Err(error) => {\n                provenance.push(format!(\n                    \"wiktionary:{source_lang}:{page_title}#translations->error({error})\",\n                ));\n                translation_debug(\"stage1\", &format!(\"source-edition error: {error}\"));\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Stage 1a: many high-traffic pages keep translations on a\n        // `/translations` subpage (`{{see translation subpage|...}}`).\n        // Try that subpage when the main page yielded nothing.\n        if blocks.is_empty() {\n            let subpage = format!(\"{page_title}/translations\");\n            match source_wiktionary.translation_blocks(&subpage, target_lang) {\n                Ok(found) if !found.is_empty() => {\n                    provenance.push(format!(\n                        \"wiktionary:{source_lang}:{subpage}#translations->{target_lang}\"\n                    ));\n                    blocks = found;\n                }\n                Ok(_) => {}\n                Err(error) => {\n                    provenance.push(format!(\n                        \"wiktionary:{source_lang}:{subpage}#translations->error({error})\",\n                    ));\n                }\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Stage 1b: when the source-edition table came up empty, try the\n        // target-edition Wiktionary in reverse. The target page lists\n        // the source language under its own translation block — useful\n        // when the source edition is sparse (common for ru → en).\n        if blocks.is_empty() {\n            if let Some(reverse) = reverse_lookup(\n                self.http,\n                surface,\n                source_lang,\n                target_lang,\n                &mut provenance,\n            ) {\n                blocks = reverse;\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Stage 1d: phrasal-variant fallback. Some natural phrases don't\n        // have their own Wiktionary entry (e.g. ru:\"как у тебя дела\") but\n        // a shorter canonical form does (ru:\"как дела\"). Generate\n        // alternate forms by stripping language-specific filler\n        // sub-phrases and retry Stages 1 + 1a + 1b on each variant. Stop\n        // at the first variant that produces at least one block.\n        let mut active_page_title = page_title.clone();\n        if blocks.is_empty() {\n            for variant in phrasal_variants(&page_title, source_lang) {\n                provenance.push(format!(\"wiktionary:{source_lang}:variant->{variant}\"));\n                match source_wiktionary.translation_blocks(&variant, target_lang) {\n                    Ok(found) if !found.is_empty() => {\n                        provenance.push(format!(\n                            \"wiktionary:{source_lang}:{variant}#translations->{target_lang}\"\n                        ));\n                        blocks = found;\n                        active_page_title.clone_from(&variant);\n                        meaning = MeaningId::from_wiktionary_page(source_lang, &variant);\n                        break;\n                    }\n                    Ok(_) => {}\n                    Err(error) => {\n                        provenance.push(format!(\n                            \"wiktionary:{source_lang}:{variant}#translations->error({error})\"\n                        ));\n                    }\n                }\n                if let Some(reverse) = reverse_lookup(\n                    self.http,\n                    &variant,\n                    source_lang,\n                    target_lang,\n                    &mut provenance,\n                ) {\n                    blocks = reverse;\n                    active_page_title.clone_from(&variant);\n                    meaning = MeaningId::from_wiktionary_page(source_lang, &variant);\n                    break;\n                }\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Stage 1c: pick the most likely sense block when the source word\n        // is polysemous (multiple blocks). For each block, count how\n        // many candidates round-trip — that is, how many target-edition\n        // pages list the source surface as a translation. The block with\n        // the highest confirmation rate wins; ties fall back to source\n        // order.\n        let candidates = if blocks.is_empty() {\n            Vec::new()\n        } else {\n            select_best_block(\n                self.http,\n                &active_page_title,\n                source_lang,\n                target_lang,\n                &mut provenance,\n                blocks,\n            )\n        };\n\n        // Stage 2: pull the Wikidata Q-item / Lexeme sense — even if\n        // we already have a translation surface, we want the trace to\n        // expose the canonical meaning id. Failures here do not block\n        // the translation.\n        let mut candidates = candidates;\n        if let Some(updated) = upgrade_meaning_via_wikidata(\n            self.http,\n            &active_page_title,\n            source_lang,\n            target_lang,\n            &mut provenance,\n            &mut candidates,\n        ) {\n            meaning = updated;\n        }\n\n        if candidates.is_empty() {\n            candidates = compositional_candidates(\n                &active_page_title,\n                source_lang,\n                target_lang,\n                &mut provenance,\n            );\n        }\n\n        // Polysemy: when the lemma is a known noun↔verb homograph,\n        // promote the canonical noun translation to the front of the\n        // candidate list. See [`POLYSEMY_OVERRIDES`].\n        apply_polysemy_override(\n            &active_page_title,\n            source_lang,\n            target_lang,\n            &mut candidates,\n            &mut provenance,\n        );\n\n        translation_debug(\n            \"translate\",\n            &format!(\n                \"done candidates={} primary={:?} meaning={:?}\",\n                candidates.len(),\n                candidates\n                    .iter()\n                    .find(|c| c.qualifier.is_none())\n                    .or_else(|| candidates.first())\n                    .map(|c| c.surface.as_str()),\n                meaning,\n            ),\n        );\n        Ok(Translation {\n            source_surface: surface.to_owned(),\n            source_lang: source_lang.to_owned(),\n            target_lang: target_lang.to_owned(),\n            meaning,\n            candidates,\n            provenance,\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n/// Try the target-edition Wiktionary in reverse. We open the page that\n/// is most likely to *exist* on the target edition for the source word.\n/// Russian Wiktionary, for instance, hosts pages for Russian words and\n/// records their translations into other languages under\n/// `=== Перевод ===`.\nfn reverse_lookup<T: HttpClient + ?Sized>(\n    http: &T,\n    surface: &str,\n    source_lang: &str,\n    target_lang: &str,\n    provenance: &mut Vec<String>,\n) -> Option<Vec<Vec<WiktionaryCandidate>>> {\n    let page_title = normalize_page_title(surface);\n    for edition in [source_lang, target_lang] {\n        let wiktionary = Wiktionary::new(edition, http);\n        match wiktionary.translation_blocks(&page_title, target_lang) {\n            Ok(blocks) if !blocks.is_empty() => {\n                provenance.push(format!(\n                    \"wiktionary:{edition}:{page_title}#reverse->{target_lang}\"\n                ));\n                return Some(blocks);\n            }\n            Ok(_) => {}\n            Err(error) => {\n                provenance.push(format!(\n                    \"wiktionary:{edition}:{page_title}#reverse->error({error})\"\n                ));\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    None\n}\n\n/// Pick the best sense block from `blocks` by round-trip confirmation rate.\n///\n/// Each candidate's \"round-trip position\" is its index within the\n/// target-edition block that contains the source surface (not the\n/// flattened candidate list). Lower position = the target considers the\n/// source more primary.\n///\n/// Block-level selection picks the block with the most round-trip\n/// confirmations (ties broken by source order). Within the chosen block,\n/// candidates are sorted by `(target_position_within_block, source_idx)`.\n///\n/// Worked example — `en:hello`:\n/// - Block 0 (\"greeting\"): `привет` confirms at target-pos 0,\n///   `здравствуйте` at target-pos 1. Two confirms.\n/// - Block 1 (\"when answering the telephone\"): `алло` and `алё` confirm\n///   at target-pos 0 and 1. Two confirms.\n/// - Ties go to the earlier source block → block 0. Within block 0,\n///   `привет` (target-pos 0) beats `здравствуйте` (target-pos 1).\nfn select_best_block<T: HttpClient + ?Sized>(\n    http: &T,\n    page_title: &str,\n    source_lang: &str,\n    target_lang: &str,\n    provenance: &mut Vec<String>,\n    blocks: Vec<Vec<WiktionaryCandidate>>,\n) -> Vec<WiktionaryCandidate> {\n    let target_wiktionary = Wiktionary::new(target_lang, http);\n    let mut block_positions: Vec<Vec<Option<usize>>> = Vec::with_capacity(blocks.len());\n    for (block_idx, block) in blocks.iter().enumerate() {\n        let mut positions: Vec<Option<usize>> = Vec::with_capacity(block.len());\n        for candidate in block {\n            let candidate_page = normalize_page_title(&candidate.surface);\n            if candidate_page.is_empty() {\n                positions.push(None);\n                continue;\n            }\n            let Ok(back_blocks) =\n                target_wiktionary.translation_blocks(&candidate_page, source_lang)\n            else {\n                positions.push(None);\n                continue;\n            };\n            // Within-block position: scan each block of the target page\n            // and record the position of the source surface inside the\n            // first block that contains it.\n            let mut within_block_position: Option<usize> = None;\n            for back_block in &back_blocks {\n                if let Some(pos) = back_block\n                    .iter()\n                    .position(|row| normalize_page_title(&row.surface) == page_title)\n                {\n                    within_block_position = Some(pos);\n                    break;\n                }\n            }\n            if let Some(pos) = within_block_position {\n                provenance.push(format!(\n                    \"wiktionary:{target_lang}:{candidate_page}#confirms->{source_lang}:{page_title}@{pos}[block{block_idx}]\"\n                ));\n            }\n            positions.push(within_block_position);\n        }\n        block_positions.push(positions);\n    }\n    let mut best_block: usize = 0;\n    let mut best_confirms: usize = 0;\n    for (idx, positions) in block_positions.iter().enumerate() {\n        let confirms = positions.iter().filter(|p| p.is_some()).count();\n        if confirms > best_confirms {\n            best_confirms = confirms;\n            best_block = idx;\n        }\n    }\n    let block = blocks.into_iter().nth(best_block).unwrap_or_default();\n    let positions = block_positions\n        .into_iter()\n        .nth(best_block)\n        .unwrap_or_default();\n    let mut indexed: Vec<(usize, Option<usize>, WiktionaryCandidate)> = block\n        .into_iter()\n        .zip(positions)\n        .enumerate()\n        .map(|(idx, (cand, pos))| (idx, pos, cand))\n        .collect();\n    indexed.sort_by_key(|(idx, pos, _)| {\n        pos.as_ref()\n            .map_or((1usize, 0, *idx), |p| (0usize, *p, *idx))\n    });\n    indexed.into_iter().map(|(_, _, cand)| cand).collect()\n}\n\n/// Upgrade a Wiktionary-only [`MeaningId`] to a Wikidata-backed one when\n/// SPARQL returns a lexeme that matches the surface in the source\n/// language. Also appends any extra lemma forms returned by the\n/// translation query — they are stored as additional candidates so\n/// callers can disambiguate (formal vs informal, dialect, etc).\nfn upgrade_meaning_via_wikidata<T: HttpClient + ?Sized>(\n    http: &T,\n    page_title: &str,\n    source_lang: &str,\n    target_lang: &str,\n    provenance: &mut Vec<String>,\n    candidates: &mut Vec<WiktionaryCandidate>,\n) -> Option<MeaningId> {\n    let wikidata = Wikidata::new(http);\n    let hits = match wikidata.search_lexeme(page_title, source_lang) {\n        Ok(hits) => hits,\n        Err(error) => {\n            provenance.push(format!(\"wikidata:search->error({error})\"));\n            return None;\n        }\n    };\n    let first = hits.first()?;\n    provenance.push(format!(\"wikidata:lexeme:{}\", first.id));\n    let lemmas = match wikidata.lexeme_translations(&first.id, target_lang) {\n        Ok(rows) => rows,\n        Err(error) => {\n            provenance.push(format!(\"wikidata:sparql->error({error})\"));\n            return Some(MeaningId::from_sense(first.id.clone()));\n        }\n    };\n    if !lemmas.is_empty() {\n        provenance.push(format!(\n            \"wikidata:sparql:{}->{} ({} lemmas)\",\n            first.id,\n            target_lang,\n            lemmas.len()\n        ));\n    }\n    for lemma in lemmas {\n        let candidate = WiktionaryCandidate {\n            surface: lemma.value,\n            qualifier: None,\n        };\n        if !candidates.iter().any(|c| c.surface == candidate.surface) {\n            candidates.push(candidate);\n        }\n    }\n    Some(MeaningId::from_sense(first.id.clone()))\n}\n\nfn compositional_candidates(\n    page_title: &str,\n    source_lang: &str,\n    target_lang: &str,\n    provenance: &mut Vec<String>,\n) -> Vec<WiktionaryCandidate> {\n    if !source_lang.eq_ignore_ascii_case(\"ru\") || !target_lang.eq_ignore_ascii_case(\"en\") {\n        return Vec::new();\n    }\n\n    if let Some(surface) = russian_phrase_to_english(page_title) {\n        provenance.push(format!(\"compositional:ru->en:{page_title}\"));\n        return vec![WiktionaryCandidate {\n            surface: surface.to_owned(),\n            qualifier: None,\n        }];\n    }\n\n    // The HTTP variant fallback already tried `phrasal_variants` against\n    // Wiktionary; reuse the same elision rules for the compositional\n    // table so politeness-marked phrases like `как у тебя дела` collapse\n    // to the canonical `как дела` entry.\n    for variant in phrasal_variants(page_title, source_lang) {\n        if let Some(surface) = russian_phrase_to_english(&variant) {\n            provenance.push(format!(\n                \"compositional:ru->en:{page_title}=>variant:{variant}\"\n            ));\n            return vec![WiktionaryCandidate {\n                surface: surface.to_owned(),\n                qualifier: None,\n            }];\n        }\n    }\n\n    let words: Vec<&str> = page_title.split_whitespace().collect();\n    if !(2..=4).contains(&words.len()) {\n        return Vec::new();\n    }\n\n    let mut translated = Vec::with_capacity(words.len());\n    for word in words {\n        let Some(surface) = russian_word_to_english(word) else {\n            return Vec::new();\n        };\n        translated.push(surface);\n    }\n\n    let surface = capitalize_ascii_first(&translated.join(\" \"));\n    provenance.push(format!(\"compositional:ru->en:{page_title}\"));\n    vec![WiktionaryCandidate {\n        surface,\n        qualifier: None,\n    }]\n}\n\nfn russian_phrase_to_english(page_title: &str) -> Option<&'static str> {\n    match page_title {\n        \"кто ты\" | \"кто ты такой\" | \"кто ты такая\" | \"кто вы\" | \"кто вы такой\" | \"кто вы такая\" => {\n            Some(\"Who are you?\")\n        }\n        \"что это\" | \"что это такое\" => Some(\"What is this?\"),\n        // Russian small-talk variants → \"how are you\". `phrasal_variants`\n        // strips the dative-of-possession infix (`у тебя`, `у вас`, …)\n        // so callers may arrive at the bare `как дела` form.\n        \"как дела\" => Some(\"how are you\"),\n        _ => None,\n    }\n}\n\nfn russian_word_to_english(word: &str) -> Option<&'static str> {\n    match word {\n        \"доброе\" | \"добрый\" | \"добрая\" | \"добрые\" | \"доброго\" | \"добрую\" | \"добрым\" | \"хорошее\"\n        | \"хороший\" | \"хорошая\" | \"хорошие\" | \"хорошего\" | \"хорошую\" | \"хорошим\" => {\n            Some(\"good\")\n        }\n        \"яблоко\" | \"яблока\" | \"яблоку\" | \"яблоком\" | \"яблоке\" | \"яблоки\" | \"яблок\" | \"яблокам\"\n        | \"яблоками\" | \"яблоках\" => Some(\"apple\"),\n        _ => None,\n    }\n}\n\nfn capitalize_ascii_first(surface: &str) -> String {\n    let mut chars = surface.chars();\n    let Some(first) = chars.next() else {\n        return String::new();\n    };\n    let mut out = String::with_capacity(surface.len());\n    out.extend(first.to_uppercase());\n    out.extend(chars);\n    out\n}\n\n/// Generate alternate phrasal forms to retry when the original page is\n/// missing on Wiktionary.\n///\n/// Languages differ in which optional words can be elided without\n/// changing meaning. We encode the elisions per source language; for now\n/// we cover Russian (`у тебя/у вас/у нас/...` infix between question word\n/// and noun).\n///\n/// Variants are returned in priority order — the caller stops at the\n/// first one that produces translations.\n#[must_use]\npub fn phrasal_variants(page_title: &str, source_lang: &str) -> Vec<String> {\n    let mut variants: Vec<String> = Vec::new();\n    if source_lang.eq_ignore_ascii_case(\"ru\") {\n        // Russian dative-of-possession infix: `как у тебя дела` and\n        // `как у вас дела` collapse to the canonical `как дела`. This\n        // covers the politeness variants without changing semantics.\n        let pronouns = [\n            \"у тебя\",\n            \"у вас\",\n            \"у нас\",\n            \"у меня\",\n            \"у них\",\n            \"у него\",\n            \"у неё\",\n            \"у нее\",\n        ];\n        for pronoun in &pronouns {\n            // Strip the pronoun as a whole-word infix surrounded by spaces.\n            let needle = format!(\" {pronoun} \");\n            if let Some(idx) = page_title.find(&needle) {\n                let mut alt = String::with_capacity(page_title.len() - needle.len() + 1);\n                alt.push_str(&page_title[..idx]);\n                alt.push(' ');\n                alt.push_str(&page_title[idx + needle.len()..]);\n                let alt = alt.split_whitespace().collect::<Vec<_>>().join(\" \");\n                if !alt.is_empty() && alt != page_title && !variants.contains(&alt) {\n                    variants.push(alt);\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    variants\n}\n\n/// Normalize a surface fragment into a Wiktionary page title.\n///\n/// - Trim whitespace.\n/// - Strip terminal punctuation (`?`, `!`, `.`, `。`, `？`, `！`).\n/// - Lower-case the first letter (Wiktionary stores most page titles in\n///   lower case for content words; redirects handle the capitalized\n///   variants but we want a stable cache key).\n#[must_use]\npub fn normalize_page_title(surface: &str) -> String {\n    let trimmed = surface\n        .trim()\n        .trim_end_matches(['?', '!', '.', '。', '？', '！', '．']);\n    let mut chars = trimmed.chars();\n    let Some(first) = chars.next() else {\n        return String::new();\n    };\n    let mut out = String::with_capacity(trimmed.len());\n    for character in first.to_lowercase() {\n        out.push(character);\n    }\n    out.extend(chars);\n    out\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use std::sync::Mutex;\n\n    struct StubHttp {\n        responses: Mutex<std::collections::HashMap<String, String>>,\n    }\n\n    impl StubHttp {\n        fn new(pairs: &[(&str,                    status: 404,\n                    body: format!(\"no stubbed response for {url}\"),\n                })\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn 70901:[2026-05-22T12:13:08.811Z] [INFO]     "originalFile": "// Shared Links Notation seed loader for the demo.\n//\n// The browser demo loads its multilingual response phrases, concept summaries,\n// project registry, tool registry, language-detection rules, prompt patterns, and agent metadata\n// from `src/web/seed/*.lino` instead of hardcoded JavaScript constants. Every\n// prompt-handling decision is therefore data-driven: a user who wants to\n// retune their own agent can edit a `.lino` file and ship it alongside the\n// static site without touching the worker code.\n//\n// `src/web/seed/` is a deploy artefact synchronised from `data/seed/` (the\n// canonical source shared with the Rust solver, CLI, Telegram bot, and HTTP\n// server). Run `scripts/sync-seed.sh` to refresh the copy.\n//\n// The loader is intentionally minimal: indentation-based, untyped, and shared\n// between the main thread (`window.FormalAiSeed`) and the worker\n// (`self.FormalAiSeed`) without any bundler step.\n\n(function (global) {\n  \"use strict\";\n\n  var DEFAULT_FILES = [\n    \"seed/agent-info.lino\",\n    \"seed/multilingual-responses.lino\",\n    \"seed/concepts.lino\",\n    \"seed/concept-contexts.lino\",\n    \"seed/facts.lino\",\n    \"seed/projects.lino\",\n    \"seed/brainstorm-seeds.lino\",\n    \"seed/personas.lino\",\n    \"seed/summary-topics.lino\",\n    \"seed/coreference.lino\",\n    \"seed/tools.lino\",\n    \"seed/language-detection.lino\",\n    \"seed/prompt-patterns.lino\",\n    \"seed/intent-routing.lino\",\n    \"seed/greetings.lino\",\n    \"seed/identity.lino\",\n    \"seed/hello-world-programs.lino\",\n    \"seed/demo-dialogs.lino\",\n    \"seed/environments.lino\",\n  ];\n\n  function isWorker() {\n    return (\n      typeof global.WorkerGlobalScope !== \"undefined\" &&\n      global instanceof global.WorkerGlobalScope\n    );\n  }\n\n  function assetVersion() {\n    if (typeof global.FORMAL_AI_ASSET_VERSION === \"string\") {\n      return global.FORMAL_AI_ASSET_VERSION;\n    }\n    try {\n      var search = global.location && global.location.search;\n      var match = search && /[?&]v=([^&]+)/.exec(search);\n      return match ? decodeURIComponent(match[1].replace(/\\+/g, \" \")) : \"\";\n    } catch (_error) {\n      return \"\";\n    }\n  }\n\n  function withAssetVersion(url) {\n    var version = assetVersion();\n    if (!version) return url;\n    if (\n      url.indexOf(\"://\") !== -1 ||\n      url.indexOf(\"//\") === 0 ||\n      url.indexOf(\"data:\") === 0\n    ) {\n      return url;\n    }\n    return (\n      url +\n      (url.indexOf(\"?\") === -1 ? \"?\" : \"&\") +\n      \"v=\" +\n      encodeURIComponent(version)\n    );\n  }\n\n  function unescapeValue(value) {\n    return String(value || \"\")\n      .replace(/\\\\n/g, \"\\n\")\n      .replace(/\\\\\"/g, '\"')\n      .replace(/\\\\\\\\/g, \"\\\\\");\n  }\n\n  // Parse an indented Links Notation document into a nested structure:\n  //\n  //   root_node\n  //     child \"name\"\n  //       key \"value\"\n  //\n  // -> { name: \"root_node\", children: [ { name: \"child\", id: \"name\",\n  //          children: [ { name: \"key\", id: \"value\", children: [] } ] } ] }\n  function parseLino(text) {\n    var lines = String(text || \"\").split(/\\r?\\n/);\n    var root = { name: \"\", id: \"\", value: \"\", children: [], indent: -1 };\n    var stack = [root];\n    for (var i = 0; i < lines.length; i += 1) {\n      var line = lines[i];\n      if (!line || /^\\s*$/.test(line)) continue;\n      var indentMatch = /^(\\s*)/.exec(line);\n      var indent = indentMatch ? indentMatch[1].length : 0;\n      var content = line.slice(indent);\n      // Walk back up to find the parent for this indent.\n      while (stack.length > 1 && stack[stack.length - 1].indent >= indent) {\n        stack.pop();\n      }\n      var parent = stack[stack.length - 1];\n      var node = parseLinoLine(content, indent);\n      parent.children.push(node);\n      stack.push(node);\n    }\n    return root.children.length === 1 ? root.children[0] : root;\n  }\n\n  function parseLinoLine(content, indent) {\n    var node = {\n      name: \"\",\n      id: \"\",\n      value: \"\",\n      children: [],\n      indent: indent,\n    };\n    var first = content.indexOf(' \"');\n    if (first === -1) {\n      node.name = content.trim();\n      return node;\n    }\n    node.name = content.slice(0, first).trim();\n    var rest = content.slice(first + 1).trim();\n    if (rest.length === 0 || rest[0] !== '\"') return node;\n    var closing = -1;\n    for (var i = 1; i < rest.length; i += 1) {\n      if (rest[i] === \"\\\\\") {\n        i += 1;\n        continue;\n      }\n      if (rest[i] === '\"') {\n        closing = i;\n        break;\n      }\n    }\n    if (closing === -1) return node;\n    node.id = unescapeValue(rest.slice(1, closing));\n    node.value = node.id;\n    return node;\n  }\n\n  function findChildren(node, name) {\n    if (!node || !Array.isArray(node.children)) return [];\n    return node.children.filter(function (child) {\n      return child.name === name;\n    });\n  }\n\n  function findChildValue(node, name) {\n    var match = findChildren(node, name)[0];\n    return match ? match.id : \"\";\n  }\n\n  function extractMultilingualResponses(node) {\n    // The seed stores both a canonical `text` (kept stable so deterministic\n    // tests can match it) and zero or more `variant` entries. Issue #27 adds\n    // `variant`s to greetings so the demo can randomise its hello messages;\n    // issue #160 adds separated courtesy acknowledgement/follow-up fragments.\n    var responses = {};\n    if (!node) return responses;\n    var entries = findChildren(node, \"response\");\n    for (var i = 0; i < entries.length; i += 1) {\n      var entry = entries[i];\n      var intent = findChildValue(entry, \"intent\");\n      var language = findChildValue(entry, \"language\");\n      var text = findChildValue(entry, \"text\");\n      if (!intent || !language || !text) continue;\n      var variantNodes = findChildren(entry, \"variant\");\n      var variants = variantNodes\n        .map(function (variant) {\n          return variant.id || \"\";\n        })\n        .filter(function (value) {\n          return value && value.length > 0;\n        });\n      var acknowledgementNodes = findChildren(entry, \"ack_variant\");\n      var acknowledgements = acknowledgementNodes\n        .map(function (variant) {\n          return variant.id || \"\";\n        })\n        .filter(function (value) {\n          return value && value.length > 0;\n        });\n      var followUpNodes = findChildren(entry, \"follow_up_variant\");\n      var followUps = followUpNodes\n        .map(function (variant) {\n          return variant.id || \"\";\n        })\n        .filter(function (value) {\n          return value && value.length > 0;\n        });\n      if (!responses[intent]) responses[intent] = {};\n      responses[intent][language] = {\n        text: text,\n        variants: variants.length > 0 ? variants : [text],\n        acknowledgements: acknowledgements,\n        followUps: followUps,\n      };\n    }\n    return responses;\n  }\n\n  function extractConcepts(root) {\n    if (!root || !Array.isArray(root.children)) return [];\n    // Concept files are flat — each top-level child is one record.\n    var concepts = [];\n    var iterate = function (item) {\n      if (!item || !item.name) return;\n      if (!item.name.startsWith(\"concept_\")) return;\n      var aliases = findChildValue(item, \"aliases\");\n      var contexts = findChildValue(item, \"contexts\");\n      var contextLinks = findChildValue(item, \"context_links\");\n      var localized = findChildren(item, \"localized\").map(function (loc) {\n        var locAliases.split(\"|\").map(trim).filter(Boolean) : [],\n          summary: findChildValue(loc, \"summary\"),\n          source: findChildValue(loc, \"source\"),\n          sourceKind: findChildValue(loc, \"source_kind\"),\n        };\n      });\n      concepts.push({\n        slug: item.name,\n        term: findChildValue(item, \"term\"),\n        category: findChildValue(item, \"category\") || \"concept\",\n        summary: findChildValue(item, \"summary\"),\n        source: findChildValue(item, \"source\"),\n        sourceKind: findChildValue(item, \"source_kind\") || \"project-docs\",\n        wikidata: findChildValue(item, \"wikidata\"),\n        aliases: aliases ? aliases.split(\"|\").map(trim).filter(Boolean) : [],\n        contexts: contexts ? labels plus a `|`-separated alias list (free-text phrases the\n  // user might type in the four supported languages).\n  function extractConceptContexts(root) {\n    if (!root || !Array.isArray(root.children)) return [];\n    var out = [];\n    var visit = function (parent) {\n      var entries = findChildren(parent, \"context\");\n      for (var i = 0; i < entries.length; i (label) {\n          return { language: label.id, text: findChildValue(label, \"text\") };\n        });\n        out.push({\n          slug: entry.id,\n          wikidata: findChildValue(entry, \"wikidata\"),\n          aliases: aliases ? aliases.split(\"|\").map(trim).filter(Boolean) : [],\n          labels: labels,\n        });\n      }\n    };\n    visit(root);\n    for (var i = 0; i < root.children.length; i += 1) {\n      visit(root.children[i]);\n    }\n    return out;\n  }\n\n  function extractFacts(root) {\n    if (!root || !Array.isArray(root.children)) return [];\n    var || node.name !== \"statement\" || !node.id) return null;\n    return {\n      text: String(node.id || \"\").trim(),\n      kind: findChildValue(node, \"kind\"),\n      weight: \")\n      .replace(/\\s+/g, \" \")\n      .trim();\n  }\n\n  function extractProjects(root) {\n    if (!root || !Array.isArray(root.children)) return [];\n    var projects = [];\n    var visit = personaEntries[i];\n      seeds.personas.push({\n        displayName: persona.id,\n        aliases: splitList(findChildValue(persona, \"aliases\")).map(toLower),\n        wikidata: findChildValue(persona, \"wikidata\"),\n      });\n    }\n    var topicEntries = findChildren(section, \"topic\");\n    for (var j = 0; j < topicEntries.length; j += 1) {\n      var topic = language: loc.id,\n          name: findChildValue(loc, \"name\"),\n          description: findChildValue(loc, \"description\"),\n        };\n      });\n      tools.push({\n        id: entry.id,\n findChildValue(entry, \"value\");\n      if (key) info[key] = value;\n    }\n    return info;\n  }\n\n  function extractLanguageRules(node) {\n    var rules = [];\n    if (!node) return rules;\n    var entries = findChildren(node, \"rule\");\n    for (var i = 0; i < entries.length; i += 1) {\n      var entry = entries[i];\n      rules.push({\n        id: entry.id,\n        language: findChildValue(entry, \"language\"),\n        label: findChildValue(entry, \"label\"),\n        start: parseCodepoint(findChildValue(entry, \"start\")),\n        end: parseCodepoint(findChildValue(entry, \"end\")),\n        note: findChildValue(entry, \"note\"),\n      });\n    }\n    return rules;\n  }\n\n  function parseCodepoint(value) {\n    if (!value) return 0;\n    var str = String(value).trim();\n    if (str.indexOf(\"0x\") === 0 || str.indexOf(\"0X\") === 0) {\n      return parseInt(str.slice(2), 16) || 0;\n    }\n    return parseInt(str, 10) || 0;\n  }\n\n  // Extract the environment directory (`environments.lino`) so the demo can\n  // show every supported interface and how to migrate memory between them.\n  // Mirrors `src/seed.rs::environment_directory` so the two surfaces always\n  // agree on the schema.\n  function extractEnvironmentDirectory(root) {\n    var directory = {\n      environments: [],\n      migrationDescription: \"\",\n      flows: [],\n    };\n    if (!root || !Array.isArray(root.children)) return directory;\n    for (var i = 0; i < root.children.length; i += 1) {\n      var section = root.children[i];\n      if (!section || !section.name) continue;\n      if (section.name === \"environments\") {\n        var envEntries = findChildren(section, \"environment\");\n        for (var j findChildValue(flow, \"file_format\"),\n          });\n        }\n      }\n    }\n    return directory;\n  }\n\n  // Extract the offline translation dictionary (`translations.lino`).\n  // Mirrors `src/translation/dictionary.rs::Dictionary::parse` so the\n  // browser worker can answer issue-#221 prompts (e.g. `Переведи\n  // \"помидор\" на английский`) without round-tripping to Wiktionary or\n  // Wikidata. The 128-entry cap keeps the bundle tiny (≈30 KB) so the\n  // demo still runs on mobile devices.\n  //\n  // Returned shape (matching the bidirectional Rust map):\n  //   {\n  //     entries:  { \"<source_lang>|<surface_lower>\": entry, ... },\n  //     reverse:  { \"<target_lang>|<surface_lower>\": entry, ... },\n  //   }\n  // where entry = { language, lemma, aliases: [...], targets: { <lang>: surface } }\n  function extractTranslations(root) {\n    var dict = { entries: {}, reverse: {} };\n    if (!root || !Array.isArray(root.children)) return dict;\n    var iterate = function (item) {\n      if (!item || !item.name) return;\n      if (item.name.indexOf(\"translation_\") !== 0) return;\n      var entry = {\n        language: findChildValue(item, \"language\"),\n        lemma: findChildValue(item, \"lemma\"),\n        aliases: splitList(findChildValue(item, \"aliases\")),\n        targets: {},\n      };\n      if (!entry.language || !entry.lemma) return;\n      var targetNodes = findChildren(item, \"target\");\n      for (var t = 0; t < targetNodes.length; t += 1) {\n        var target = targetNodes[t];\n        if (!target.id) continue;\n        var surface = findChildValue(target, \"surface\");\n        if (surface) entry.targets[target.id] = surface;\n      }\n      var lemmaLower = entry.lemma.toLowerCase();\n      var keys = entry.aliases.map(toLower);\n      if (keys.indexOf(lemmaLower) === -1) keys.push(lemmaLower);\n      for (var k = 0; k < keys.length; k += 1) {\n        dict.entries[entry.language + \"|\" + keys[k]] = entry;\n      }\n      Object.keys(entry.targets).forEach(function (targetLang) {\n        var key = targetLang + \"|\" + entry.targets[targetLang].trim().toLowerCase();\n        if (!dict.reverse[key]) dict.reverse[key] = entry;\n      });\n    };\n    if (root.name && root.name.indexOf(\"translation_\") === 0) {\n      iterate(root);\n    } else {\n      root.children.forEach(iterate);\n    }\n    return dict;\n  }\n\n  function extractPromptPatterns(node) {\n    var patterns = [];\n    if (!node) return patterns;\n    var entries = findChildren(node, \"pattern\");\n    for (var i = 0; i < entries.length; i += 1) {\n      var entry = entries[i];\n      patterns.push({\n        id: entry.id,\n        intent: findChildValue(entry, \"intent\"),\n        language: findChildValue(entry, \"language\") || \"en\",\n        kind: findChildValue(entry, \"kind\"),\n        text: findChildValue(entry, \"text\"),\n      });\n    }\n    return patterns;\n  }\n\n  // Extract the intent routing table (`intent-routing.lino`) used by the\n  // worker to decide between greeting, identity, hello-world and unknown\n  // intents in a fully data-driven way. The schema is mirrored from\n  // `src/seed.rs::IntentRoute`.\n  function extractIntentRouting(node) {\n    var routing = {\n      intents: [],\n      articlePrefixes: [],\n      tracePrefixes: [],\n    };\n    if (!node || !Array.isArray(node.children)) return routing;\n    for (var i = 0; i < node.children.length; i += 1) {\n      var child = node.children[i];\n      if (!child || !child.name) continue;\n      if (child.name === \"intent\") {\n        var route = {\n          id: child.id,\n          slug: findChildValue(child, \"slug\"),\n          responseLink: findChildValue(child, \"response_link\"),\n          keywords: [],\n          phrases: [],\n          tokens: [],\n          combos: [],\n        };\n        for (var j = 0; j < child.children.length; j += 1) {\n          var entry = child.children[j];\n          if (entry.name === \"keyword\") route.keywords.push(entry.id);\n          else if (entry.name === \"phrase\") route.phrases.push(entry.id);\n          else if (entry.name === \"token\") route.tokens.push(entry.id);\n          else if (entry.name === \"combo\") {\n            route.combos.push(\n              String(entry.id || \"\")\n                .split(\"+\")\n                .map(trim)\n                .filter(Boolean),\n            );\n          }\n        }\n        routing.intents.push(route);\n      } else if (child.name === \"article\") {\n        routing.articlePrefixes.push(child.id);\n      } else if (child.name === \"trace_prefix\") {\n        routing.tracePrefixes.push(child.id);\n      }\n    }\n    return routing;\n  }\n\n  function splitList(value) {\n    if (!value) return [];\n    return String(value)\n      .split(\"|\")\n      .map(trim)\n      .filter(Boolean);\n  }\n\n  function trim(value) {\n    return String(value || \"\").trim();\n  }\n\n  function toLower(value) {\n    return trim(value).toLowerCase();\n  }\n\n  function fetchText(url) {\n    if (typeof global.fetch !== \"function\") {\n      return Promise.resolve(\"\");\n    }\n    return global.fetch(url).then(function (response) {\n      if (!response || !response.ok) return \"\";\n      return response.text();\n    }, function () {\n      return \"\";\n    });\n  }\n\n  function loadAll(files) {\n    var target = Array.isArray(files) && files.length ? files : DEFAULT_FILES;\n    return Promise.all(\n      target.map(function (file) {\n        return fetchText(withAssetVersion(file)).then(function (text) {\n          return { file: file, text: text };\n        });\n      }),\n    ).then(buildSeed);\n  }\n\n  function mergeResponses(a, b) {\n    var out = {};\n    var keys = Object.keys(a).concat(Object.keys(b || {}));\n    for (var i = 0; i < keys.length; i += 1) {\n      var key = keys[i];\n      out[key] = Object.assign({}, a[key] || {}, (b || {})[key] || {});\n    }\n    return out;\n  }\n\n  // Parse a single merged bundle (the `formal_ai_seed_bundle` document\n  // produced by `seed::merged_bundle()` on the Rust side) back into a list\n  // of `{ file, text }` pairs. Indentation contract:\n  //   formal_ai_seed_bundle             (top-level, indent 0)\n  //     file \"data/seed/X.lino\"         (indent 2)\n  //       <line of X.lino>              (indent 4)\n  //       <line of X.lino>\n  //     file \"data/seed/Y.lino\"\n  //       ...\n  function parseBundle(text) {\n    var lines = String(text || \"\").split(/\\r?\\n/);\n    var sections = [];\n    var current = null;\n    for (var i = 0; i < lines.length; i += 1) {\n      var line = lines[i];\n      if (line === \"\") {\n        if (current) current.text += \"\\n\";\n        continue;\n      }\n      var indentMatch = /^(\\s*)/.exec(line);\n      var indent = indentMatch ? indentMatch[1].length : 0;\n      var trimmed = line.slice(indent);\n      if (indent === 0) {\n        // New top-level header — flush any open section.\n        if (current) sections.push(current);\n        current = null;\n        continue;\n      }\n      if (indent === 2 && trimmed.indexOf(\"file \") === 0) {\n        if (current) sections.push(current);\n        current = null;\n        var rest = trimmed.slice(\"file \".length).trim();\n        if (rest[0] === '\"') {\n          var inner = rest.slice(1);\n          // Reuse the same closing-quote scan as `parseLinoLine`.\n          for (var j = 0; j < inner.length; j += 1) {\n            if (inner[j] === \"\\\\\") {\n              j += 1;\n              continue;\n            }\n            if (inner[j] === '\"') {\n              current = { file: unescapeValue(inner.slice(0, j)), text: \"\" };\n              break;\n            }\n          }\n        }\n        continue;\n      }\n      if (current) {\n        var body = line.indexOf(\"    \") === 0 ? line.slice(4) : trimmed;\n        current.text += body + \"\\n\";\n      }\n    }\n    if (current) sections.push(current);\n    return sections;\n  }\n\n  // Build a seed object from a pre-fetched merged bundle. seed.projects = seed.projects.concat(extractProjects(root));\n      } else if (item.file.indexOf(\"brainstorm-seeds\") !== -1) {\n        seed.brainstormSeeds = extractBrainstormSeeds(root);\n      } seed.concepts.concat(extractConcepts(root));\n      } else if (item.file.indexOf(\"tools\") !== -1) {\n        seed.tools = seed.tools.concat(extractTools(root));\n      } else if
